Each circle has a radius of 4\u2009arcsec and is centred where the counter-image is predicted to be, which, because of prediction errors, is not necessarily exactly on the counter-image candidate(s). In the blue and purple area, the plausible counter-images Abell 2261-14000 and Abell 2261-1366, respectively, were identified. In the grey area, no plausible counter-images were found.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx157fig2.jpg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/60310659/stx157fig2.jpg\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx157fig2.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"60310659\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/467/1/10.1093_mnras_stx157/2/stx157fig2.jpeg?Expires=1639262684&Signature=xXMommmfXIcxkCYzuhdUy9UfxL8ZzWZbo3mIDI41oFaFugkr8yWhZfwJaBEKFhwF0w4EMoRJoR3Rk8sUetgtj2EQZMry~tYvZyjYHyJAygeHUZfu6FYoTWcnJdaVZtzlqyT9wjkrNmxW2burDP3CHBsL9JN~ofScLvcRkMx6nMQcakMPG1lIWO3Lzk9Mgs88RbB0GPc6UdB7kQUS771FzG7PTS0mpG9C3f~F-KRZDHbKx0e38nDFylw2~ABcCbDW4r9Uqx1waNaWY2hZL4nKhgukX8GO5Xr6pune3mBpS~nkxyyeihg2Cz1VBjHnAk972MlX2d1mB~O4kxWfmqTECw__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=60310659&ar=2961791&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx157fig2.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">100\u2009arcsec\u00a0\u00d7\u00a0100\u2009arcsec overviews. The left-hand panel is a multicolour image of Abell 2261 (<em>F606W</em> is represented by blue, <em>F814W</em> is represented by green and <em>F125W</em> is represented by red) of Abell 2261. The critical line for <em>z</em><sub>s</sub>\u00a0=\u00a06.3 is marked in white. The right-hand image is a magnification map for Abell 2261 (Zitrin et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib85\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib85\" data-open=\"bib85\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015a</a>), colour-coded to show the magnification for a source at <em>z</em><sub>s</sub>\u00a0=\u00a06.3. The originally identified object, Abell 2261-910, and a second nearby object, Abell 2261-911 (treated together as one object, Abell 2261-9000), at a similar photometric redshift, are marked by a red circle. The regions where counter-images were predicted to be are marked in blue, purple and grey. Each circle has a radius of 4\u2009arcsec and is centred where the counter-image is predicted to be, which, because of prediction errors, is not necessarily exactly on the counter-image candidate(s). In the blue and purple area, the plausible counter-images Abell 2261-14000 and Abell 2261-1366, respectively, were identified. In the grey area, no plausible counter-images were found.</p></div></div>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=60310660 id=\"60310660\" class=\"section-title js-splitscreen-section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec5-2>5.2 Abell 2261-1467 and Abell 2261-1468</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">In the area predicted to contain a counter-image marked by blue in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>, the official catalogues contained eight objects. Of these, all but two either had redshifts that were too low or were too faint (the detections were all below 5\u03c3), and none had morphologies corresponding to Abell 2261-910/Abell 2261-911. The remaining two, Abell 2261-1467 and Abell 2261-1468, of which the former has been published in Bradley et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib8\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib8\" data-open=\"bib8\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>), are close enough to the predicted location to be the counter-image of Abell 2261-9000, including the binary substructure. The images are 1.7 and 0.9\u2009arcsec for Abell 2261-1467 and Abell 2261-1468, respectively, from the predicted location. For the same reason as for the Abell 2261-9000 system, Abell 2261-1467 and Abell 2261-1468 are treated as a single object \u2013 hereafter Abell 2261-14000. Like Abell 2261-9000, Abell 2261-14000 has 5\u03c3 detections in <em>F850LP</em> as well as all IR filters, even 10\u03c3 in <em>F105W</em>, <em>F110W</em> and <em>F140W</em>.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=60310662 id=\"60310662\" class=\"section-title js-splitscreen-section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec5-3>5.3 Abell 2261-1366</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">In the official catalogues, seven objects exist within 4.0\u2009arcsec (within the purple circle in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>) of the second counter-image's predicted position. One of them is a star covering a large fraction of the area where the counter-image is predicted. One is another fainter star, and four are either too faint or do not have matching morphologies, photometric redshifts and/or colours. The last object, Abell 2261-1366 (previously published in Bradley et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib8\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib8\" data-open=\"bib8\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>), found 3.2\u2009arcsec from the position of the predicted counter-image, does correspond sufficiently well to Abell 2261-9000 and Abell 2261-14000 to be reliably considered as a counter-image.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Abell 2261-1366 appears as an extended arc parallel to the critical curve (compare Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig3\" data-open=\"fig3\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">3</a> to Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>) in the IR filters except <em>F105W</em> (and to some extent in <em>F850LP</em>) where substructure can be discerned. Abell 2261-1366 has 5\u03c3 detections in all IR filters, except for a 10\u03c3 detection in <em>F110W</em>. As opposed to Abell 2261-9000 and Abell 2261-14000, Abell 2261-1366 is not detected in <em>F850LP</em>; the difference is discussed in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec5-7\"></span><a href=\"#sec5-7\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec js-xref-sec\">5.7</a>. This non-detection means that the SED fitting uses five filters instead of six, and the image being slightly fainter is the plausible reason for its higher photometric redshift of 6.8 and a generally lower quality of fit compared to Abell 2261-9000 and Abell 2261-14000. Its higher photometric redshift does not make it incompatible as a counter-image since its quality of fit is almost as good at the photometric redshifts corresponding to Abell 2261-9000 and Abell 2261-14000.</p>                        <a id=\"60310665\" scrollto-destination=\"60310665\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig3\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 3.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/467/1/10.1093_mnras_stx157/2/m_stx157fig3.jpeg?Expires=1639262684&amp;Signature=Lrd-eq23FzOrwzoficGxCX7lZbXl2lqjxlogEM~WWjtBieiOd-UczeXHP9NnjA~sg1F5EKTd99xLCtQe8eJZBQ~AF0UgZu-Tz6UkRsdT72oNJwmHiRa46qX6qjb5iDOibHVe7gE3oS8tFMBoh5WHv5LQ1gR4DHEhNL94x19CtdKgS6THMYj0a9qHgoBn69eW8aLH4D8SyfzIPMH7~qH~WJOrn1xnRwsmcDYGtfb2b0zQKKkgZZSw4yjk-37Gg5Z~O2ekGyZpGvb9v7RJQ4wecJTk7pOOmsWIUfUzbqnh5GgbB531AZ1XR5Fg2qF0mVLOUDnyUstVMICW7DIyZszhTQ__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"3.3\u2009arcsec\u00a0\u00d7\u00a03.3\u2009arcsec thumbnail images of the counter-images. First column: multicolour thumbnails of the three counter-images (blue: F850LP; green: F125W; F160W: red). Abell 2261-14000s thumbnail image's blue part is brighter and also larger compared to Abell 2261-9000 and Abell 2261-1366. The blue part also connects the substructure, implying that it could be a Ly\u00a0\u03b1 halo. Abell 2261-1366 is polluted by a nearby star, which makes the thumbnail background bright. Column 2\u20138: In the black and white thumbnails, the colours are inverted. Each column represents one of the seven filters with wavelengths relevant for z\u00a0&gt;\u00a06 objects. The Ly\u00a0\u03b1-break is evident between the filters F814W and F850LP for Abell 2261-9000 and Abell 2261-14000 but not as clearly for Abell 2261-1366. For all three objects, hints of flux can be discerned in F814W, which could be spurious detections or a smaller fraction of the spectrum visible in the filter. There are some substructures for Abell 2261-9000 and Abell 2261-14000 (each was originally identified as two objects) in the form of two detected objects, each in F125W, F140W and F160W, marked by the red circles. In the shorter wavelength filters, the objects look more like extended arcs. For Abell 2261-1366, the substructure is not as clearly identifiable but can be seen in F105W and to some extent in F850LP, and it resembles an arc in the other IR filters. The uppermost third object seen in Abell 2261-9000 was identified as a low-redshift interloper, a conclusion strengthened by the fact that only two objects are observed in Abell 2261-14000. In the filters F105W, F110W and F140W, for Abell 2261-9000, an object can also be seen in the lower part of the thumbnails. However, it is significantly fainter than the other objects, and its data and model fits do not correspond well to the other objects, so we discard it as a part of Abell 2261-9000. Comparing the extended arcs/substructures of the objects to Fig.\u00a02, they can be seen to be parallel to the critical curve. This implies that the gravitational lensing could be the source of the extension/increase in the separation of the substructure.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx157fig3.jpg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/60310665/stx157fig3.jpg\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx157fig3.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"60310665\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/467/1/10.1093_mnras_stx157/2/stx157fig3.jpeg?Expires=1639262684&Signature=NWS5H-EgZr-GS4XWmjDBE4fJnAFtAjjNhssodCru2r4aowHvV13UC8Fs~MuhJTme8eeDMWYf1lDDFBr31bAchrAJ1cfOyWdAdne-wKhQYeIA8TtPEEcTw35Ku2jVT3RrLMOnC-s-NLhzNJAll-GvjWVhRimamIBOckzdwsojZJtKK6exSnrCVQooBH1fv0n57Z~wbjrrrWuWT3875ECyuHog1aEHOTW1JNdUHNh-Jw1cU-RX679a3MrRtK-GznrDIwB19HBbjrL6g8H-1ZXLIGwR62mRjC9HkQL~Gr1MiECByw6~SA4qMImH2oqBtqOoqtusFbSX5Bd0-naOFNqrzQ__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=60310665&ar=2961791&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx157fig3.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">3.3\u2009arcsec\u00a0\u00d7\u00a03.3\u2009arcsec thumbnail images of the counter-images. Column 2\u20138: In the black and white thumbnails, the colours are inverted. Each column represents one of the seven filters with wavelengths relevant for <em>z</em>\u00a0&gt;\u00a06 objects. Comparing the extended arcs/substructures of the objects to Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>, they can be seen to be parallel to the critical curve. This implies that the gravitational lensing could be the source of the extension/increase in the separation of the substructure.</p></div></div><div content-id=\"fig3\" class=\"fig fig-modal reveal-modal\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 3.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/467/1/10.1093_mnras_stx157/2/m_stx157fig3.jpeg?Expires=1639262684&amp;Signature=Lrd-eq23FzOrwzoficGxCX7lZbXl2lqjxlogEM~WWjtBieiOd-UczeXHP9NnjA~sg1F5EKTd99xLCtQe8eJZBQ~AF0UgZu-Tz6UkRsdT72oNJwmHiRa46qX6qjb5iDOibHVe7gE3oS8tFMBoh5WHv5LQ1gR4DHEhNL94x19CtdKgS6THMYj0a9qHgoBn69eW8aLH4D8SyfzIPMH7~qH~WJOrn1xnRwsmcDYGtfb2b0zQKKkgZZSw4yjk-37Gg5Z~O2ekGyZpGvb9v7RJQ4wecJTk7pOOmsWIUfUzbqnh5GgbB531AZ1XR5Fg2qF0mVLOUDnyUstVMICW7DIyZszhTQ__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"3.3\u2009arcsec\u00a0\u00d7\u00a03.3\u2009arcsec thumbnail images of the counter-images. The blue part also connects the substructure, implying that it could be a Ly\u00a0\u03b1 halo. Abell 2261-1366 is polluted by a nearby star, which makes the thumbnail background bright. Column 2\u20138: In the black and white thumbnails, the colours are inverted. Each column represents one of the seven filters with wavelengths relevant for <em>z</em>\u00a0&gt;\u00a06 objects. The Ly\u00a0\u03b1-break is evident between the filters <em>F814W</em> and <em>F850LP</em> for Abell 2261-9000 and Abell 2261-14000 but not as clearly for Abell 2261-1366. For all three objects, hints of flux can be discerned in <em>F814W</em>, which could be spurious detections or a smaller fraction of the spectrum visible in the filter. There are some substructures for Abell 2261-9000 and Abell 2261-14000 (each was originally identified as two objects) in the form of two detected objects, each in <em>F125W</em>, <em>F140W</em> and <em>F160W</em>, marked by the red circles. In the shorter wavelength filters, the objects look more like extended arcs. For Abell 2261-1366, the substructure is not as clearly identifiable but can be seen in <em>F105W</em> and to some extent in <em>F850LP</em>, and it resembles an arc in the other IR filters. The uppermost third object seen in Abell 2261-9000 was identified as a low-redshift interloper, a conclusion strengthened by the fact that only two objects are observed in Abell 2261-14000. In the filters <em>F105W</em>, <em>F110W</em> and <em>F140W</em>, for Abell 2261-9000, an object can also be seen in the lower part of the thumbnails. However, it is significantly fainter than the other objects, and its data and model fits do not correspond well to the other objects, so we discard it as a part of Abell 2261-9000. Comparing the extended arcs/substructures of the objects to Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>, they can be seen to be parallel to the critical curve. This implies that the gravitational lensing could be the source of the extension/increase in the separation of the substructure.</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">The most plausible alternative explanation to Abell 2261-1366 being a counter-image would be that the brightest star, which obstructs a circular area <em>r</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a01\u2009<em>arcsec</em>, hides the counter-image.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=60310667 id=\"60310667\" class=\"section-title js-splitscreen-section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec5-4>5.4 The third predicted counter-image</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The grey circle in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a> marks the third predicted counter-image. The official catalogues contain nine objects within 4.0\u2009arcsec of the predicted counter-image. Four of the objects are so faint (S/N\u00a0&lt;\u00a05 in all filters) as to be flagged as spurious detections in the official catalogues. Three objects are stars and the last two objects have a too low photometric redshift. Since the predicted magnifications, \u03bc\u00a0\u223c\u00a02.5, in the region are lower than for the other regions, the counter-image is expected to be fainter. The magnitudes of the fainter objects, <em>m</em><sub>AB</sub>\u00a0\u223c\u00a028.5, are barely consistent with those of the other counter-images when considering the magnification including errors.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">There are two possibilities for the counter-image: either it is one of the fainter objects and the magnification is significantly different from the calculated one (but still barely within the error bars) or it is behind one of the foreground stars. Since their morphology does not correspond to that of either Abell 2261-9000, Abell 2261-14000 or Abell 2261-1366 (as there are no two faint objects close by), we will not consider the fainter objects further.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=60310670 id=\"60310670\" class=\"section-title js-splitscreen-section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec5-5>5.5 Joint analysis of the three counter-images</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">In addition to examining each image individually and comparing them, we analyse them as one object. We sum the fluxes of all three of them in each filter, henceforth called Abell 2261-stacked. Abell 2261-stacked is constructed directly from observed values. We have also de-lensed the observations before stacking them which yields nearly identical results. One drawback of this approach is that the fitting might be dominated by one image, especially if it is significantly brighter. This means the fit might be good for only one image. However, our three counter-images have roughly similar magnifications and magnitudes. Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl2\" data-open=\"tbl2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a> lists the coordinates of the objects (including the stacked object) and their AB-magnitudes in the seven longest wavelength CLASH filters. It also contains the redshift, metallicity, the \u03c7<sup>2</sup> value of the fit and the model-implied rest-frame EW(Ly\u00a0\u03b1) corrected for ISM/IGM absorption using <em>f</em><sub>Ly\u2009\u03b1</sub>. The magnification estimated with the gravitational lens model is also included (Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec5-7\"></span><a href=\"#sec5-7\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec js-xref-sec\">5.7</a>). class=\"chapter-para\">The <em>P</em>(<em>z</em>) and <em>P</em>(<em>f</em><sub>Ly\u2009\u03b1</sub>) quantities, i.e. the photometric-redshift distribution and the photometric-<em>f</em><sub>Ly\u2009\u03b1</sub> distribution, are calculated using the cross-validation technique described in Rydberg et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib61\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib61\" data-open=\"bib61\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>). For each <em>z</em> or <em>f</em><sub>Ly\u2009\u03b1</sub>, the model (for the considered grid) with the highest cross-validation value (i.e. quality of fit) is selected. A good quality of fit for a certain grid thus means that there is at least one model in the grid that fits the observations well. The cross-validation value is normalized to the interval [0, 1] (where 1 implies that each data point is perfectly reproduced by the model), and is used as a proxy for a probability distribution.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">In Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig4\" data-open=\"fig4\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">4</a>, each row corresponds to one of the three objects Abell 2261-9000, Abell 2261-14000 and Abell 2261-1366, as well as the stacked version, Abell 2261-stacked. The observational data and spectrum of the best-fitting model for each grid are listed in the first column, while the second column shows the <em>P</em>(<em>z</em>) from different model grids.</p>                        <a id=\"60310675\" scrollto-destination=\"60310675\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig4\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 4.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/467/1/10.1093_mnras_stx157/2/m_stx157fig4.jpeg?Expires=1639262684&amp;Signature=Lqltp6bnBxSv3kzKi75eBYOAgmkYDWSSl8YyIZyhcJaTrGP47b9RVMf8~FpmGmueqsVPQ1GeunsvPN9-Y~giMgI9-CHNMyOuTc1kM8aS5rCDJmpUobaGK3ysQoc4Tn0mesxo0tp81-LdVYmIXS20K8DpwnOuY2B4Wnkk-FVLuN6~nHG~B8WsRbM067M6aNzKkaTSbf~DBe~sQ8-mxD0gP-ZW8iFjwIYZBQdITR07koXKJChBDn6vhbLSHVPbup9dTBuo70ehTo1Z~3EATxzi3VFAUQxJxgIaQBG6lQtiKij4EDwsz-NMT~na8MWC0N9J10gu36OE4Swr5O-RmSTQPg__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Left-hand column: magnitudes and synthetic spectra of the best-fitting model for each grid. The other two images and the stacked image have significantly smaller uncertainties.</p></div></div>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=60310676 id=\"60310676\" class=\"section-title js-splitscreen-section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec5-6>5.6 Constraints from non-<em>HST</em> observations</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">To rule out old and/or dusty objects, data from four <em>Spitzer</em> filters were examined (Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec2-1\"></span><a href=\"#sec2-1\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec js-xref-sec\">2.1</a>). Visual inspection yielded no detections in these filters. This strengthens the case for the high-redshift solutions since low-redshift dusty (<em>E</em>(<em>B</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>V</em>)<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn4\" data-open=\"fn4\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\"><sup>4</sup></a> \u2273 0.3, when dust attenuation is implemented on Yggdrasil models) objects would be visible in the <em>Spitzer</em> 3.6- and/or 4.5-mm filters. For objects at the same <em>z</em> as the photometric redshift of our object, both extremely dusty objects and old galaxies would be visible and thus are ruled out.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Extremely strong optical emission lines (such as [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] lines) from low-redshift objects can affect broad-band photometry SED fitting and mimic a high-redshift Ly\u00a0\u03b1 line (Huang et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib30\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib30\" data-open=\"bib30\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>). But since there is continuum data for this candidate at longer wavelengths and it registers as a non-detection at wavelengths shorter than the Ly\u00a0\u03b1-break, it is likely not due to a strong non-Ly\u00a0\u03b1 emission line from a faint object. Huang et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib30\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib30\" data-open=\"bib30\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) has conducted a search for extremely strong emission-line galaxies of this type in CLASH and our candidate is not among those they identified, further strengthening the conclusion that our results are not due to strong optical emission lines. Furthermore, our spectroscopic observations, which show no prominent detections in the <em>J</em> band (Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec2-2\"></span><a href=\"#sec2-2\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec js-xref-sec\">2.2</a>), disfavour strong [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] or [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] from objects at <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a02.1\u20134.8.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=60310679 id=\"60310679\" class=\"section-title js-splitscreen-section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec5-7>5.7 Counter-image comparison</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">When considering different images as counter-images of the same object, the images have to be consistent with regard to redshift as well as morphology and fluxes (including magnification).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">As a first step, we analyse Abell 2261-stacked (Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec5-5\"></span><a href=\"#sec5-5\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec js-xref-sec\">5.5</a>). We find a best fit at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a06.3, with good quality fits extending from <em>z</em><sub>L</sub> \u2248 5.6 to <em>z</em><sub>U</sub> \u2248 6.5 and EW(Ly\u00a0\u03b1) \u2248160 \u00c5. The most plausible redshift is 6.3 for the Yggdrasil Z\u00a0&gt;\u00a00 grid as well with essentially equally good fits. Hence, there are alternatives to the Pop III interpretation of the object. The Gissel and CWW, Kinney grids are not considered further because their <em>P</em>(<em>z</em>) are significantly lower than those of the Yggdrasil grids. Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig5\" data-open=\"fig5\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">5</a> contains the quality of fits dependence on <em>f</em><sub>Ly\u2009\u03b1</sub> for Abell 2261-stacked at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a06.3. It is evident that both Yggdrasil grids have a strong dependence on <em>f</em><sub>Ly\u2009\u03b1</sub>.</p>                        <a id=\"60310682\" scrollto-destination=\"60310682\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig5\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 5.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/467/1/10.1093_mnras_stx157/2/m_stx157fig5.jpeg?Expires=1639262684&amp;Signature=bQB~NagZ94eE1PPA8raltoJKTaAaGHNM6OlqwQTsv8ZFi22JrNgc8NFZ1WC44gFCmsmsRZrHQoVEz3k2bMM4V4rIbt-p9wBZOjzyBmdPZj~Hgkz6MSbJZlObdW0OS~5Ud-r~jGcq6EjM53llqWSd7TWi3tnxU7YSFzXchaYQy9-ttNiMeNoufUCL4CL7CI83V0gTRyGr3nJrKSADNnYRTWsHSudsoR5ku5mQlzZA4aIsLIfFjLNLzYHNHSp0hwD8UtI0~KBKTcy1cMTdvX7wS06osJjhK-vN9IXi2~s8mql36kT-Jh31VPrX075RFxD9huaTyFbMqFh1m1P8W5z6aQ__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"The quality of fit as a function of the Ly\u00a0\u03b1 escape fraction fLy\u2009\u03b1 at z\u00a0=\u00a06.3. It has a strong dependence on fLy\u2009\u03b1. The Pop III model grid allows a lower fLy\u2009\u03b1 with a high quality of fit. The Yggdrasil Z\u00a0&gt;\u00a00 model grid is more sensitive to fLy\u2009\u03b1, and since galaxies with metals are more likely to contain dust, the fLy\u2009\u03b1 might be low. This could mean that there is a (admittedly weak) case for it to be metal-free, or at least have a very low metallicity.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx157fig5.jpg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/60310682/stx157fig5.jpg\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx157fig5.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"60310682\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/467/1/10.1093_mnras_stx157/2/stx157fig5.jpeg?Expires=1639262684&Signature=GCcXjk2nxOlr025BMXqtiG5UdcEogR4ovsppcmbCBVfO-s2Hik9z42n5FR17w44eiHWOpHUUEAvBDDc1KtG-6umb4ZOKXKyFrirVtrvAgZMWX2JOQbCTcQZpkRCQO96MV6Bk9cQzIkuEv7ix6cL5jrEIVnhvtWbY9exUghn80H2GpTFfDsR120drwdYmZjDaTNubmpKpQe~HXY4jfZRW7EMc3hKmgfmlSuuOcAB39STTzEbIwBZx~9nYMkFY6cfs1AzXpWSSCFdQ~aKUxOjGHNIyhJswn03Rs9kXNoSCAFUr0XKBCFuUuMuRGwA2nLpuAOOUBtKr1X2XUvLOnEccDg__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=60310682&ar=2961791&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx157fig5.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">The quality of fit as a function of the Ly\u00a0\u03b1 escape fraction <em>f</em><sub>Ly\u2009\u03b1</sub> at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a06.3. It has a strong dependence on <em>f</em><sub>Ly\u2009\u03b1</sub>. The Pop III model grid allows a lower <em>f</em><sub>Ly\u2009\u03b1</sub> with a high quality of fit. The Yggdrasil Z\u00a0&gt;\u00a00 model grid is more sensitive to <em>f</em><sub>Ly\u2009\u03b1</sub>, and since galaxies with metals are more likely to contain dust, the <em>f</em><sub>Ly\u2009\u03b1</sub> might be low. This could mean that there is a (admittedly weak) case for it to be metal-free, or at least have a very low metallicity.</p></div></div><div content-id=\"fig5\" class=\"fig fig-modal reveal-modal\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 5.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/467/1/10.1093_mnras_stx157/2/m_stx157fig5.jpeg?Expires=1639262684&amp;Signature=bQB~NagZ94eE1PPA8raltoJKTaAaGHNM6OlqwQTsv8ZFi22JrNgc8NFZ1WC44gFCmsmsRZrHQoVEz3k2bMM4V4rIbt-p9wBZOjzyBmdPZj~Hgkz6MSbJZlObdW0OS~5Ud-r~jGcq6EjM53llqWSd7TWi3tnxU7YSFzXchaYQy9-ttNiMeNoufUCL4CL7CI83V0gTRyGr3nJrKSADNnYRTWsHSudsoR5ku5mQlzZA4aIsLIfFjLNLzYHNHSp0hwD8UtI0~KBKTcy1cMTdvX7wS06osJjhK-vN9IXi2~s8mql36kT-Jh31VPrX075RFxD9huaTyFbMqFh1m1P8W5z6aQ__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"The quality of fit as a function of the Ly\u00a0\u03b1 escape fraction fLy\u2009\u03b1 at z\u00a0=\u00a06.3. The Yggdrasil Z\u00a0&gt;\u00a00 model grid is more sensitive to fLy\u2009\u03b1, and since galaxies with metals are more likely to contain dust, the fLy\u2009\u03b1 might be low. This could mean that there is a (admittedly weak) case for it to be metal-free, or at least have a very low metallicity.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx157fig5.jpg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/60310682/stx157fig5.jpg\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx157fig5.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"60310682\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/467/1/10.1093_mnras_stx157/2/stx157fig5.jpeg?Expires=1639262684&Signature=GCcXjk2nxOlr025BMXqtiG5UdcEogR4ovsppcmbCBVfO-s2Hik9z42n5FR17w44eiHWOpHUUEAvBDDc1KtG-6umb4ZOKXKyFrirVtrvAgZMWX2JOQbCTcQZpkRCQO96MV6Bk9cQzIkuEv7ix6cL5jrEIVnhvtWbY9exUghn80H2GpTFfDsR120drwdYmZjDaTNubmpKpQe~HXY4jfZRW7EMc3hKmgfmlSuuOcAB39STTzEbIwBZx~9nYMkFY6cfs1AzXpWSSCFdQ~aKUxOjGHNIyhJswn03Rs9kXNoSCAFUr0XKBCFuUuMuRGwA2nLpuAOOUBtKr1X2XUvLOnEccDg__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=60310682&ar=2961791&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx157fig5.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">The quality of fit as a function of the Ly\u00a0\u03b1 escape fraction <em>f</em><sub>Ly\u2009\u03b1</sub> at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a06.3. It has a strong dependence on <em>f</em><sub>Ly\u2009\u03b1</sub>. The Pop III model grid allows a lower <em>f</em><sub>Ly\u2009\u03b1</sub> with a high quality of fit. The Yggdrasil Z\u00a0&gt;\u00a00 model grid is more sensitive to <em>f</em><sub>Ly\u2009\u03b1</sub>, and since galaxies with metals are more likely to contain dust, the <em>f</em><sub>Ly\u2009\u03b1</sub> might be low. This could mean that there is a (admittedly weak) case for it to be metal-free, or at least have a very low metallicity.</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig6\" data-open=\"fig6\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">6</a> compares the magnitudes of the three counter-images after de-lensing them using our magnification estimates. We see that Abell 2261-14000 is approximately 1.0\u00a0mag brighter (a factor of 2.5) than Abell 2261-9000 and Abell 2261-1366 after de-lensing. But the errors in the magnification estimates, which are systematic across the filters, are large and the discrepancies are within the errors. The observations in <em>F850LP</em>, however, have too large a difference to be explained by magnification errors. Also, when comparing the colours in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig6\" data-open=\"fig6\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">6</a>, the observations in the IR filters are consistent with an SED with a declining slope, while only the <em>F850LP</em> observation for Abell 2261-9000 is consistent with this SED. The <em>F850LP</em> magnitudes of Abell 2261-14000 and Abell 2261-1366 are much brighter and fainter, respectively. This poses a challenge for the interpretation but it could possibly be explained by an extended Ly\u00a0\u03b1 halo around the galaxy. The sensitivity of the detector could be such that the halo is only detected if the object is bright enough, and would hence contribute a disproportionate amount of flux if the object is brighter. The flux is consistent with this scenario because it is significantly higher in the brightest image Abell 2261-14000, compared to Abell 2261-9000 and Abell 2261-1366. The reason Abell 2261-1366 differs from Abell 2261-9000 could be that Abell 2261-1366 is contaminated by light from the nearby star, rendering the halo indistinguishable from the illumination provided by the star.</p>                        <a id=\"60310684\" scrollto-destination=\"60310684\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig6\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 6.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/467/1/10.1093_mnras_stx157/2/m_stx157fig6.jpeg?Expires=1639262684&amp;Signature=wXXBWoWHSWvct~M60IBSL~6wz34WIWf1qgjTS68AT17i6QCovRK~yWs5qLmgkoKsP7pCNEkcaqcxJzmzI7IXQFglgMRETgntzXanFqxOVJd4P3uoXi5af9wphEmD8BeDWQSAN1lJXKCI9LCFwJcbxM2ylohu8PN6N3mAOJwhgIpb6Zla~tVVC2yYCX4AqSE9fw912Sql5DXAj1TCEeAi3J9~d4AM99hcqqOzi6-oKHRCTTgEOHZ~a8Jy5su-Y0TVxzb36-z-~oBb3ivZKnhamyU0fM7tB7Qs2TyiBeD22qEYDM7l3Ohn6RxUMczcvFyAa3c25IqlLpK0q9-Pm1IVMA__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"AB-magnitudes for the three images de-lensed with our magnification estimates. Abell 2261-1366 is polluted by a nearby star, which makes the background bright, possibly rendering the Ly\u00a0\u03b1 halo indistinguishable from the background and thus unobserved. The observational trends in the other filters, i.e. being fainter with wavelength in IR, holds for the different images. However, Abell 2261-14000 is \u223c1 AB-magnitude lower than the other counter-images, or about a factor of 2.5 brighter. The errors in magnifications are systematic, and large enough to bridge the differences in magnitude between the images.</p></div></div>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=60310685 id=\"60310685\" class=\"section-title js-splitscreen-section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec5-8>5.8 Interacting galaxies?</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">To constitute a merger or a virialized galaxy, the substructure must be within the virialized radius of the DM halo. Hence, if the distance between the two clumps is larger than twice the virialized radius, the two clumps are neither a part of the same object nor in the process of becoming one, even though a future collision might produce a merger. The lowest stellar mass suggested by our models for this structure is \u223c10<sup>6</sup>\u2009M<sub>\u2299</sub>. If 15\u00a0per\u00a0cent of the halo mass is baryonic and all the baryons reside in stars (in reality, only a small fraction do, which would imply an even more massive halo), the halo would be\u00a0\u223c7\u00a0\u00d7\u00a010<sup>6</sup> M<sub>\u2299</sub>. We take the virialized mass of the structure to be <em>M</em><sub>200</sub>, the mass enclosed by the radius at which the density is 200\u00a0times the critical density, which also corresponds to the virialized radius R<sub>200</sub>. For <em>M</em><sub>200</sub>\u00a0\u223c\u00a07\u00a0\u00d7\u00a010<sup>6</sup>\u2009M<sub>\u2299</sub>, <em>R</em><sub>200</sub>\u00a0=\u00a0800\u00a0pc. Since we assume the minimum mass for the DM halo, this is the lower limit to its virialized radius.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The angular distances between the centres of substructure in the three images (0.60\u00a0arcsec for Abell 2261-9000, 0.87\u2009arcsec for Abell 2261-14000 and 1.2\u2009arcsec for Abell 2261-1366), which correspond to de-lensed separations of \u2273370\u00a0pc at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a06.3. Since the distance between the substructures along the sightline is unknown, this should be taken as a lower limit. Comparing this to the minimum virialized radius <em>R</em><sub>200</sub>\u00a0=\u00a0800\u00a0pc, we conclude that the clumps could be close enough to be virialized, and therefore substructure in a galaxy or an interaction/merger.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The proximity of the clumps could indicate a galaxy merger (Lin et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib42\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib42\" data-open=\"bib42\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2004</a>) but could also be a chance projection of two high-redshift objects whose actual separation along the sightline is too large for a merger. However, given the similarities in morphology, estimated redshift and colours between the three images, it is unlikely they could be chance projections. The AB-magnitude increase due to greater separations would have to be compensated by correspondingly lower luminosity. The angular size of the substructures are also roughly equal, which would have to be a coincidence if the substructure were a chance projection. Because our current data cannot constrain collision angle or speed, composition (which we have assumed to be the same in our combined fitting) or relative mass, further investigation is required to determine if the lensed object is a merger.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=60310689 id=\"60310689\" class=\"section-title js-splitscreen-section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec6>6 SUMMARY AND CONCLUSION</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">We have discovered a likely multiply lensed LAE candidate with three counter-images, Abell 2261-9000, Abell 2261-14000 and Abell 2261-1366, with magnifications <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\mu \\sim 4.3^{+1.6}_{-1.7}{}$|\u2060</span>, <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$3.7^{+1.3}_{-1.3}{}$|</span> and <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$5.5^{+2.4}_{-2.3}{}$|\u2060</span>, respectively. Another image is predicted but is not detected. In the process of locating the counter-images, we measured the first spectroscopic redshift (<em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a03.377) of a multiply imaged galaxy behind Abell 2261, which was used to calibrate the lensing model. Using this in combination with the photometric redshifts of our three images, we conclude that it is likely that the three images are of the same object. The LAE was initially considered to be a Pop III galaxy candidate but competitive fits with non-zero metallicity models indicate that other interpretations are equally likely. By combining these fits using Yggdrasil models, a redshift estimate of 6.3 was obtained for the galaxy. This redshift estimate is dependent on the assumption of strong Ly\u00a0\u03b1 emission. Future observations targeting Ly\u00a0\u03b1 in these objects will soon be able to test these predictions.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">In two of the counter-images, substructure appearing as two objects in the same orientation expected from the lens model were found in the filters with the longest wavelengths. The substructure could also be discerned in the third image, even though it was not separable into two objects. They could be star-forming regions belonging to the same galaxy or two interacting galaxies. SED fitting of models to photometry implies extreme Ly\u00a0\u03b1 emission, with EW(Ly\u00a0\u03b1) \u223c160 \u00c5. We also find that the angular distance between its substructures is not too large for them to be a single virialized structure or a merger between two small galaxies. The kinematics of the structures could not be constrained with current observations but might be with additional surveys. Follow-up observations could target any of the lines: [C\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] (Knudsen et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib40\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib40\" data-open=\"bib40\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>), [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] (Inoue et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib34\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib34\" data-open=\"bib34\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>), [C\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span>] (Stark et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib72\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib72\" data-open=\"bib72\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015b</a>) and/or C\u00a0<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] (Stark et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib71\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib71\" data-open=\"bib71\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015a</a>). Given a detection, splitting in the observed line would indicate large relative velocities that may indicate a recent merger.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">If confirmed through spectroscopy, this galaxy would join a rising number of LAEs now being discovered at <em>z</em>\u00a0&gt;\u00a06. Similar objects at higher redshifts may be the birthplaces of direct collapse black holes, the likely precursors of the most massive black holes at <em>z</em>\u00a0&gt;\u00a06 (Mortlock et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib46\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib46\" data-open=\"bib46\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>; Wu et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib77\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib77\" data-open=\"bib77\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>). Others, as may be true of CR7, may harbour Pop III stars. CLASH, Frontier Fields and future surveys of cluster lenses may reveal these objects and yield clues to the origins of the first stars and supermassive black holes in the Universe.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=60310693 id=\"60310693\" class=\"backacknowledgements-title js-splitscreen-backacknowledgements-title\" >Acknowledgments</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">CER acknowledges funding from the Swedish National Space Board and the Royal Swedish Academy of Sciences.
